TENTATIVI: 0
CODICE:
import pandas as pd

# Load the datasets using exact paths provided
happiness_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')
cost_of_living_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# Sort happiness data by Score descending and select top 5
top_happiness = happiness_df.sort_values(by='Score', ascending=False).head(5)

# Merge the datasets using left_on and right_on to handle column name mismatches
merged_df = pd.merge(
    top_happiness,
    cost_of_living_df,
    left_on='Country or region',
    right_on='Country',
    how='inner'
)

# Handle empty results or NaNs in the target column
# If the merge results in an empty dataframe or all NaNs in the cost of living index, print error
if merged_df.empty or merged_df['Cost of Living Index'].isna().any():
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Select relevant columns for the final output
    result = merged_df[['Country or region', 'Score', 'Cost of Living Index']]
    print(result)

OUTPUT:
Country or region  Score  Cost of Living Index
0           Finland  7.769                  63.2
1           Denmark  7.600                  72.3
2            Norway  7.554                  76.0
3           Iceland  7.494                  83.0
4       Netherlands  7.488                  63.1

import pandas as pd

# Load the happiness data (2019.csv)
happiness_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')

# Load the LPI data (Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv)
lpi_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# Preprocess country columns to handle case sensitivity (Constraint 7)
happiness_df['Country or region'] = happiness_df['Country or region'].str.lower()
lpi_df['Country'] = lpi_df['Country'].str.lower()

# Filter happiness scores above 6
happiness_filtered = happiness_df[happiness_df['Score'] > 6]

# Filter LPI below 50
lpi_filtered = lpi_df[lpi_df['Local Purchasing Power Index'] < 50]

# Merge the filtered dataframes on country names
merged_df = pd.merge(happiness_filtered, lpi_filtered, left_on='Country or region', right_on='Country', how='inner')

# Calculate the count
count = len(merged_df)

# Handle empty results (Constraint 8)
if count == 0:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(count)

file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Pokemon.csv'

# Filter for Fire-type Pokémon (case-insensitive)

# Check if any records were found

    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")

    # Sort by Attack stat in descending order and select top 5
    top_5_fire = fire_pokemon.sort_values(by='Attack', ascending=False).head(5)

import pandas as pd

# Load the avocado dataset
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/avocado.csv')

# Filter for year 2017
df = df[df['year'] == 2017]

# Filter for region Chicago (case-insensitive)
df = df[df['region'].str.lower() == 'chicago']

# Filter for type organic (case-insensitive)
df = df[df['type'].str.lower() == 'organic']

# Check if dataframe is empty or if average price is NaN
if df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    avg_cost = df['AveragePrice'].mean()
    if pd.isna(avg_cost):
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
    else:
        print(f"The average cost of organic avocados sold in Chicago in 2017 was: {avg_cost}")

OUTPUT:
The average cost of organic avocados sold in Chicago in 2017 was: 1.8233962264150942

import pandas as pd

file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv'

try:
    df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

    # Check if required columns exist to avoid KeyError
    if 'Groceries Index' in df.columns and 'Rent Index' in df.columns:
        # Filter rows where Groceries Index is higher than Rent Index
        # Note: Columns are numeric, so no string case conversion needed
        mask = df['Groceries Index'] > df['Rent Index']
        count = mask.sum()

        # Handle empty results as per instructions
        if count == 0:
            print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
        else:
            print(f"Number of countries with Groceries Index higher than Rent Index: {count}")
    else:
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: Required columns not found")

except Exception as e:
    print(f"ERROR: {e}")

OUTPUT:
Number of countries with Groceries Index higher than Rent Index: 121

import pandas as pd

# Load the datasets using exact paths
happiness_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')
cost_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# Sort by happiness score and get top 5
top_5 = happiness_df.sort_values('Score', ascending=False).head(5)

# Defensive string handling: Convert country columns to lowercase for merging
# This ensures case-insensitive matching between the two datasets
top_5['Country or region'] = top_5['Country or region'].str.lower()
cost_df['Country'] = cost_df['Country'].str.lower()

# Merge the datasets on country names
merged_df = pd.merge(top_5, cost_df, left_on='Country or region', right_on='Country', how='inner')

# Handle potential NaN results in the cost column
# If the merge results in rows with NaN for Cost of Living Index, we treat it as an error per Rule 8
merged_df = merged_df.dropna(subset=['Cost of Living Index'])

# Check if the final result is empty
if merged_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Select relevant columns for the final output
    final_output = merged_df[['Country or region', 'Score', 'Cost of Living Index']]
    print(final_output)

OUTPUT:
Country or region  Score  Cost of Living Index
0           finland  7.769                  63.2
1           denmark  7.600                  72.3
2            norway  7.554                  76.0
3           iceland  7.494                  83.0
4       netherlands  7.488                  63.1

import pandas as pd

file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2017.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

if df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Filter out rows with NaN in the target columns to ensure clean data
    df_valid = df.dropna(subset=['Happiness.Score', 'Health..Life.Expectancy.'])
    
    if df_valid.empty:
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
    else:
        # Sort by both metrics ascending to identify the lowest scores
        df_sorted = df_valid.sort_values(['Happiness.Score', 'Health..Life.Expectancy.'], ascending=[True, True])
        
        # Select the bottom 5 nations
        result = df_sorted.head(5)
        
        # Print the result
        print(result[['Country', 'Happiness.Score', 'Health..Life.Expectancy.']])

150                    Rwanda            3.471                  0.326425

import pandas as pd

file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv'

try:
    df = pd.read_csv(file_path)
    
    # Filter rows where Groceries Index is strictly greater than Rent Index
    # Using boolean mask to count matching rows
    mask = df['Groceries Index'] > df['Rent Index']
    count = mask.sum()
    
    # Handle empty results or zero matches as per instructions
    if count == 0:
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
    else:
        print(count)
        
except FileNotFoundError:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
except Exception as e:
    print(f"ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")

CODICE:
import pandas as pd

# Load the happiness data
happiness_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')

# Load the cost of living data
cost_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# Merge the two dataframes on country names
# Using left_on and right_on to handle column name differences
merged_df = pd.merge(happiness_df, cost_df, left_on='Country or region', right_on='Country', how='inner')

# Check if merge resulted in any data
if merged_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Sort by happiness score in descending order
    merged_df = merged_df.sort_values(by='Score', ascending=False)

    # Select top 5 countries
    top_5 = merged_df.head(5)

    # Select relevant columns for the output
    # Using 'Country or region' as the country identifier
    result = top_5[['Country or region', 'Score', 'Cost of Living Index']]

    # Handle NaN values in Cost of Living Index
    # If any NaNs exist in the target column, drop those rows to avoid printing NaN
    result = result.dropna(subset=['Cost of Living Index'])

    # Check if result is empty after dropping NaNs
    if result.empty:
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
    else:
        print(result)

OUTPUT:
Country or region  Score  Cost of Living Index
0           Finland  7.769                  63.2
1           Denmark  7.600                  72.3
2            Norway  7.554                  76.0
3           Iceland  7.494                  83.0
4       Netherlands  7.488                  63.1

CODICE:
import pandas as pd

# Load the happiness data
df_happiness = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')

# Load the cost of living data
df_cost = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# Normalize country names to handle potential mismatches (case sensitivity, whitespace)
df_happiness['Country or region'] = df_happiness['Country or region'].str.strip().str.lower()
df_cost['Country'] = df_cost['Country'].str.strip().str.lower()

# Merge the two tables on country names
# Using left_on and right_on to specify the different column names for the join keys
merged_df = pd.merge(df_happiness, df_cost, left_on='Country or region', right_on='Country', how='inner')

# Drop the 'Country' column from the cost dataframe to avoid duplicate column names in the result
# We keep 'Country or region' from the happiness dataframe
merged_df = merged_df.drop(columns=['Country'], errors='ignore')

# Sort by happiness score in descending order
merged_df = merged_df.sort_values(by='Score', ascending=False)

# Select top 5 countries
top_5 = merged_df.head(5)

# Check if the result is empty
if top_5.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Display the relevant columns: Country, Score, Cost of Living Index
    print(top_5[['Country or region', 'Score', 'Cost of Living Index']])

OUTPUT:

0           finland  7.769                  63.2
1           denmark  7.600                  72.3
2            norway  7.554                  76.0
3           iceland  7.494                  83.0
4       netherlands  7.488                  63.1

CODICE:
import pandas as pd

# Load the datasets using exact paths
happiness_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')
cost_of_living_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# Merge the datasets on country names
# Using left_on and right_on to handle column name mismatches ('Country or region' vs 'Country')
merged_df = pd.merge(happiness_df, cost_of_living_df, left_on='Country or region', right_on='Country', how='inner')

# Drop rows with missing values in the key metrics to ensure clean output
merged_df = merged_df.dropna(subset=['Score', 'Cost of Living Index'])

# Sort by happiness score in descending order
merged_df = merged_df.sort_values(by='Score', ascending=False)

# Select the top 5 countries
top_5_countries = merged_df.head(5)

# Check if the result is empty
if top_5_countries.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Select relevant columns for the final output
    result = top_5_countries[['Country or region', 'Score', 'Cost of Living Index']]
    # Print the result clearly
    print(result.to_string(index=False))

           Norway  7.554                  76.0
          Iceland  7.494                  83.0
      Netherlands  7.488                  63.1

CODICE:
import pandas as pd

# Load the happiness data
df_happiness = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')

# Load the LPI data
df_lpi = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# Normalize country names to handle case sensitivity (Rule 7)
df_happiness['Country or region'] = df_happiness['Country or region'].str.lower()
df_lpi['Country'] = df_lpi['Country'].str.lower()

# Merge the two datasets on country names (Rule 3 & 4)
merged_df = pd.merge(
    df_happiness,
    df_lpi,
    left_on='Country or region',
    right_on='Country',
    how='inner'
)

# Filter for Happiness Score > 6 and LPI < 50
filtered_df = merged_df[
    (merged_df['Score'] > 6) & 
    (merged_df['Local Purchasing Power Index'] < 50)
]

# Count the matching countries
count = len(filtered_df)

# Handle empty results (Rule 8)
if count == 0:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(count)

OUTPUT:
12

CODICE:
import pandas as pd

file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Pokemon.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# Filter Fire-type Pokémon (Defensive with strings)
fire_pokemon = df[df['Type 1'].str.lower() == 'fire']

# Sort by Attack descending and get top 5
top_5_fire = fire_pokemon.sort_values(by='Attack', ascending=False).head(5)

# Handle empty results
if top_5_fire.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(top_5_fire[['Name', 'Attack']])

import pandas as pd

# Load the avocado dataset
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/avocado.csv')

# Filter for the year 2017
df_2017 = df[df['year'] == 2017]

# Filter for Chicago (case-insensitive)
df_chicago = df_2017[df_2017['region'].str.lower() == 'chicago']

# Filter for organic avocados (case-insensitive)
df_organic = df_chicago[df_chicago['type'].str.lower() == 'organic']

# Calculate the average price
avg_cost = df_organic['AveragePrice'].mean()

# Handle empty results or NaN values
if pd.isna(avg_cost):
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(f"The average cost of organic avocados sold in Chicago in 2017 was: {avg_cost}")

import pandas as pd

file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv'

try:
    df = pd.read_csv(file_path)
    
    # Check if required columns exist to avoid errors
    if 'Groceries Index' in df.columns and 'Rent Index' in df.columns:
        # Filter rows where Groceries Index is higher than Rent Index
        # Note: Numeric comparison does not require string lowercasing
        mask = df['Groceries Index'] > df['Rent Index']
        count = mask.sum()
        
        # Handle empty results or NaN as per instructions
        if pd.isna(count) or count == 0:
            print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
        else:
            print(count)
    else:
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: Required columns not found in the dataset")
        
except Exception as e:
    print(f"ERROR: {e}")

import pandas as pd

file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv'

df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# Filter rows where Groceries Index is higher than Rent Index
filtered_df = df[df['Groceries Index'] > df['Rent Index']]

# Count the number of countries
count = filtered_df['Country'].count()

# Handle empty results
if count == 0:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(count)

import pandas as pd

# Load the happiness dataset
happiness_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')

# Load the cost of living dataset
cost_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# Sort happiness scores in descending order to get the top countries
happiness_df = happiness_df.sort_values('Score', ascending=False)

# Select the top 5 countries
top_5_happiness = happiness_df.head(5)

# Handle potential naming mismatches by converting country columns to lowercase for merging
top_5_happiness['Country or region'] = top_5_happiness['Country or region'].str.lower()
cost_df['Country'] = cost_df['Country'].str.lower()

# Merge the top 5 happiness data with the cost of living data
merged_df = pd.merge(top_5_happiness, cost_df, left_on='Country or region', right_on='Country', how='inner')

# Check if the merge resulted in an empty dataframe
if merged_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Select the relevant columns for the final output
    result = merged_df[['Country or region', 'Score', 'Cost of Living Index']]
    print(result)

1           denmark  7.600                  72.3
2            norway  7.554                  76.0
3           iceland  7.494                  83.0
4       netherlands  7.488                  63.1

CODICE:
import pandas as pd

# Load the datasets using exact paths
df_happiness = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')
df_lpi = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# Merge the datasets on country names
# Handle naming mismatch: 'Country or region' vs 'Country'
merged_df = pd.merge(
    df_happiness,
    df_lpi,
    left_on='Country or region',
    right_on='Country',
    how='inner'
)

# Filter for happiness score > 6 and Local Purchasing Power Index < 50
filtered_df = merged_df[
    (merged_df['Score'] > 6) &
    (merged_df['Local Purchasing Power Index'] < 50)
]

# Count the number of matching countries
count = len(filtered_df)

# Handle empty results
if count == 0:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(count)

OUTPUT:
12

import pandas as pd

# Load the data using the exact path provided
file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Pokemon.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# Filter for Fire-type Pokémon using defensive string handling (Rule 7)
# Convert column to lowercase and filter for 'fire'
fire_pokemon = df[df['Type 1'].str.lower() == 'fire']

# Handle empty results (Rule 8)
if fire_pokemon.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Sort by Attack stat in descending order and select the top 5
    top_5_fire = fire_pokemon.sort_values(by='Attack', ascending=False).head(5)
    
    # Print the final answer clearly (Rule 5)
    print(top_5_fire[['Name', 'Attack']])

import pandas as pd

file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/avocado.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# Filter for year 2017
df_filtered = df[df['year'] == 2017]

# Filter for region Chicago (case-insensitive)
df_filtered = df_filtered[df_filtered['region'].str.lower() == 'chicago']

# Filter for type Organic (case-insensitive)
df_filtered = df_filtered[df_filtered['type'].str.lower() == 'organic']

# Calculate average price
avg_cost = df_filtered['AveragePrice'].mean()

# Handle empty results
if pd.isna(avg_cost):
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(f"The average cost of organic avocados sold in Chicago in 2017 was {avg_cost:.2f}")

OUTPUT:
The average cost of organic avocados sold in Chicago in 2017 was 1.82

CODICE:
import pandas as pd

file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv'

try:
    df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

    # Check if required columns exist
    if 'Groceries Index' not in df.columns or 'Rent Index' not in df.columns:
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: Required columns not found in the dataset.")
    else:
        # Ensure numeric types to handle potential non-numeric values safely
        df['Groceries Index'] = pd.to_numeric(df['Groceries Index'], errors='coerce')
        df['Rent Index'] = pd.to_numeric(df['Rent Index'], errors='coerce')

        # Filter condition
        mask = df['Groceries Index'] > df['Rent Index']
        count = mask.sum()

        # Handle NaN results as per instructions
        if pd.isna(count):
            print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
        else:
            print(f"Number of countries with Groceries Index higher than Rent Index: {count}")

except FileNotFoundError:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: File not found.")
except Exception as e:
    print(f"ERROR_EMPTY: An error occurred - {e}")

OUTPUT:
Number of countries with Groceries Index higher than Rent Index: 121

CODICE:
import pandas as pd

file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2017.csv'

try:
    df = pd.read_csv(file_path)
    
    if df.empty:
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
    else:
        # Check if required columns exist
        required_columns = ['Country', 'Happiness.Score', 'Health..Life.Expectancy.']
        missing_columns = [col for col in required_columns if col not in df.columns]
        
        if missing_columns:
            print("ERROR_EMPTY: Required columns not found in the dataset")
        else:
            # Sort by both metrics ascending to find the lowest scores
            df_sorted = df.sort_values(by=['Happiness.Score', 'Health..Life.Expectancy.'], ascending=[True, True])
            
            # Drop rows with NaN in the relevant columns to avoid printing NaN
            df_sorted = df_sorted.dropna(subset=['Happiness.Score', 'Health..Life.Expectancy.'])
            
            if df_sorted.empty:
                print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
            else:
                # Select the top 5 nations with the lowest scores
                result = df_sorted.head(5)[['Country', 'Happiness.Score', 'Health..Life.Expectancy.']]
                print(result)
except FileNotFoundError:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: File not found at the specified path")
except Exception as e:
    print(f"ERROR_EMPTY: An error occurred while processing the data: {e}")

OUTPUT:

153                   Burundi            2.905                  0.151611
152                  Tanzania            3.349                  0.364509
151                     Syria            3.462                  0.500533
150                    Rwanda            3.471                  0.326425

import pandas as pd

# Load data using exact paths
df_2015 = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2015.csv')
df_2019 = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')

# Merge tables on country columns (Rule 3)
# Use left_on and right_on to handle naming mismatches (Rule 4)
merged_df = pd.merge(df_2015, df_2019, left_on='Country', right_on='Country or region', suffixes=('_2015', '_2019'))

# Filter for Italy using lowercase comparison (Rule 7)
italy_data = merged_df[merged_df['Country'].str.lower() == 'italy']

# Handle empty results (Rule 8)
if italy_data.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for Italy in the requested years.")
else:
    # Extract scores
    score_2015 = italy_data['Happiness Score_2015'].iloc[0]
    score_2019 = italy_data['Score_2019'].iloc[0]

    # Check for NaN values before comparison
    if pd.isna(score_2015) or pd.isna(score_2019):
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for Italy in the requested years.")
    else:
        # Compare scores
        improved = score_2019 > score_2015
        print(f"Italy's happiness score in 2015 was {score_2015} and in 2019 was {score_2019}. Did it improve? {improved}")

CODICE:
import pandas as pd

# Read both CSV files
italy_2015 = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2015.csv')
italy_2019 = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')

# Filter for Italy in each file
italy_2015 = italy_2015[italy_2015['Country'] == 'Italy']
italy_2019 = italy_2019[italy_2019['Country or region'] == 'Italy']

# Get happiness scores
score_2015 = italy_2015['Happiness Score'].iloc[0]
score_2019 = italy_2019['Score'].iloc[0]

# Compare and print result
if score_2019 > score_2015:
    print(f"Italy's happiness score improved from {score_2015:.2f} in 2015 to {score_2019:.2f} in 2019.")
elif score_2019 < score_2015:
    print(f"Italy's happiness score decreased from {score_2015:.2f} in 2015 to {score_2019:.2f} in 2019.")
else:
    print(f"Italy's happiness score remained the same at {score_2015:.2f} in both 2015 and 2019.")

OUTPUT:
Italy's happiness score improved from 5.95 in 2015 to 6.22 in 2019.

import pandas as pd

file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/avocado.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

filtered_df = df[
    (df['year'] == 2017) &
    (df['type'].str.lower() == 'organic') &
    (df['region'].str.lower() == 'chicago')
]

if filtered_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    avg_cost = filtered_df['AveragePrice'].mean()
    if pd.isna(avg_cost):
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
    else:
        print(f"The average cost of organic avocados sold in Chicago in 2017 was: {avg_cost}")

OUTPUT:
The average cost of organic avocados sold in Chicago in 2017 was: 1.8233962264150942

CODE:
import pandas as pd

# Load the datasets
df_score = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')
df_cost = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# Normalize country names for merging to handle case sensitivity
df_score['country_key'] = df_score['Country or region'].str.lower()
df_cost['country_key'] = df_cost['Country'].str.lower()

# Merge the datasets on the normalized country keys
merged_df = pd.merge(df_score, df_cost, left_on='country_key', right_on='country_key', how='inner')

# Check if the merge resulted in an empty dataframe
if merged_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Find the row with the highest score
    max_score_row = merged_df.loc[merged_df['Score'].idxmax()]

    # Check if the Local Purchasing Power Index is NaN
    if pd.isna(max_score_row['Local Purchasing Power Index']):
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
    else:
        print(f"Country: {max_score_row['Country or region']}, Local Purchasing Power Index: {max_score_row['Local Purchasing Power Index']}")

OUTPUT:
Country: Finland, Local Purchasing Power Index: 118.0

import pandas as pd

# Load the datasets
df_score = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')
df_cost = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# Normalize country names for merging to handle case sensitivity
df_score['country_key'] = df_score['Country or region'].str.lower()
df_cost['country_key'] = df_cost['Country'].str.lower()

# Merge the datasets on the normalized country keys
merged_df = pd.merge(df_score, df_cost, left_on='country_key', right_on='country_key', how='inner')

# Check if the merge resulted in an empty dataframe
if merged_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Find the row with the highest score
    max_score_row = merged_df.loc[merged_df['Score'].idxmax()]

    # Check if the Local Purchasing Power Index is NaN
    if pd.isna(max_score_row['Local Purchasing Power Index']):
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
    else:
        print(f"Country: {max_score_row['Country or region']}, Local Purchasing Power Index: {max_score_row['Local Purchasing Power Index']}")
